## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed corpus-process bullets stand beside what the gate implies for failure handling, a failed gate row is not retried into submission, command failures route to diagnosis and code change before rerun, verification findings route to fixes rather than waivers, and repeated failures of the same row across changes signal an upstream doctrine or training gap, not a reason to loosen the row
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because gates create retry pressure by design, every failure blocks a delivery someone wants shipped, so the gate's integrity depends on rules for what failure may and may not trigger, fix and rerun yes, trim and pass no
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the erosion path is retry-by-weakening, a red clippy run answered by allowing the lint, a failed bundle answered by skipping the command, each converting a finding into a permanent gate reduction
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: failure-response doctrine for this gate's operation, application-level retry engineering belongs to the system design theme
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the response rules, rerun only after a change, waive only section 1 rows with reasons, and escalate repeated same-row failures to doctrine review rather than gate adjustment
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the gate needs backpressure in the queueing sense, when many changes fail the same row, the correct pressure release is upstream, better patterns taught earlier in the skill's read order, not downstream loosening, mirroring how load shedding protects a service by refusing work rather than degrading correctness

## Section 022: Observability Checklist
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed generic records stand beside the gate's own observability demands, section 3 requires verifying that no secrets or sensitive payloads are logged, section 2 pushes long-running work onto channels or binary responses whose progress is inherently observable, and sidecar supervision requires startup checks and bounded waits, which are liveness observations by definition
- **supporting_reason:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a desktop app's observability risk inverts the server case, logs live on user machines where leaked secrets persist beyond operator reach, so the gate's first logging rule is subtractive, verify absence of sensitive payloads, before any additive telemetry
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: importing server logging habits, log everything and filter later, ships user-resident files containing tokens and payloads that no log-retention policy can recall
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: observability rules the gate enforces plus this node's own audit records, application telemetry design belongs to the doctrine and system design themes
- **revision_decision:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the three observable surfaces the gate checks, log content hygiene, channel-based progress visibility, and sidecar liveness, each with its verification form
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the gate treats observability as a bounded resource on the desktop, event spam is rejected not just for performance but because unbounded emission is unobservable emission, a flooded event channel hides the signal it was meant to carry, aligning the payload rule with the logging rule under one economy-of-signal principle

- **current_section_observation:** Section 022 "Observability Checklist", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to verify log hygiene subtractively, route progress through channels, and give every sidecar a liveness check before gating a change as done

## Section 023: Performance Verification Method
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed latency packet stands beside the gate's performance stance, performance is gated structurally rather than by benchmark, no blocking work in async command contexts protects runtime responsiveness, channels or binary responses for high-volume payloads protect IPC throughput, plugin-store limited to small structured state protects storage latency, and bounded sidecar waits protect startup time
- **supporting_reason:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because desktop responsiveness dies by architecture rather than by hot loops, a blocked async runtime freezes every command at once, so the gate checks the structural properties whose violation no later optimization can repair
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: benchmark-first performance review passes structurally doomed designs, an event-spam progress stream benchmarks fine at test volumes and collapses at user volumes
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 023 "Performance Verification Method", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the gate's structural performance checks, quantitative budgeting method belongs to the system design theme's latency doctrine

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement

- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because a terminal gate scales by repetition rather than by expansion, applying the same bounded checklist to every change, and the design keeps each application cheap precisely by refusing to grow the file's scope
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: scope creep is the scale failure, gate files that accrete project lore grow until walks take hours and teams route around them, the file's compression and its section 7 self-limits are the documented defense

- **revision_decision:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to state the three boundaries, per-change application, per-project convention locality, and the rationale line where doctrine takes over
